# Add Evaluation Metadata Field to Flipt (Proto + Go)

**Repository:** flipt-io/flipt
**Access Scope:** You may modify files in `rpc/flipt/evaluation/` (protobuf schema + generated code) and `internal/server/evaluation/` (Go server). You may read any other files to understand existing patterns.

## Context

Flipt is a feature flag platform built with Go and gRPC. Its API is defined in Protocol Buffer (`.proto`) files, with generated Go code alongside. The evaluation server constructs protobuf response objects returned to clients.

Operators have requested that evaluation responses include a `segment_match_type` field so clients can see whether the evaluation matched a segment using `ALL` (all constraints matched) or `ANY` (at least one constraint matched) logic. This information is already available in the evaluation flow but is not exposed in the response.

## Task

Add a `segment_match_type` string field to the evaluation responses. This requires changes to **both** the protobuf schema (`.proto` file) and the Go server code that constructs responses — a cross-language change.

**YOU MUST IMPLEMENT CODE CHANGES.**

### Requirements

1. **Protobuf schema change** — Add `string segment_match_type` to the `VariantEvaluationResponse` message in the evaluation proto file. Determine the next sequential tag by examining existing fields in the message. The value should be "ALL", "ANY", or "" (empty when no segment matched).

2. **Generated Go code change** — Add the corresponding `SegmentMatchType string` field and getter method to the Go generated code (`.pb.go` file). Match the exact patterns used by existing fields. Do NOT regenerate code with protoc — manually add the field.

3. **Server code change** — In the evaluation server, populate `SegmentMatchType` on the response after evaluation logic determines which rule matched. The evaluation must set this field for variant evaluations, and batch responses should include it too.

4. **Determine the source value** — The storage layer carries segment operator information on evaluation rules that indicates ALL vs ANY. Find this type and trace how the operator maps to the string values you need.

## Success Criteria

- Evaluation proto has `segment_match_type` field in `VariantEvaluationResponse`
- Generated Go code has matching `SegmentMatchType` field and getter
- Server code populates `SegmentMatchType` from the rule's segment operator
- Proto tag number is valid (no collision with existing fields)
- Changes span both proto and Go files (cross-language change)
- Go code compiles: `go build ./internal/server/evaluation/...`

    13→func (s *Store) GetEvaluationRules(ctx context.Context, flag storage.ResourceRequest) (_ []*storage.EvaluationRule, err error) {
    14→	ruleMetaRows, err := s.builder.
    15→		Select("id, \"rank\", segment_operator").
    16→		From("rules").
    17→		Where(sq.Eq{"flag_key": flag.Key, "namespace_key": flag.Namespace()}).
    18→		QueryContext(ctx)
    19→	if err != nil {
    20→		return nil, err
    21→	}
    22→
    23→	defer func() {
    24→		if cerr := ruleMetaRows.Close(); cerr != nil && err == nil {
    25→			err = cerr
    26→		}
    27→	}()
    28→
    29→	type RuleMeta struct {
    30→		ID              string
    31→		Rank            int32
    32→		SegmentOperator flipt.SegmentOperator
    33→	}
    34→
    35→	var rmMap = make(map[string]*RuleMeta)
    36→
    37→	ruleIDs := make([]string, 0)
    38→	for ruleMetaRows.Next() {
    39→		var rm RuleMeta
    40→
    41→		if err := ruleMetaRows.Scan(&rm.ID, &rm.Rank, &rm.SegmentOperator); err != nil {
    42→			return nil, err
    43→		}
    44→
    45→		rmMap[rm.ID] = &rm
    46→		ruleIDs = append(ruleIDs, rm.ID)
    47→	}
    48→
    49→	if err := ruleMetaRows.Err(); err != nil {
    50→		return nil, err
    51→	}
    52→
    53→	if err := ruleMetaRows.Close(); err != nil {
    54→		return nil, err
    55→	}

    57→	rows, err := s.builder.Select(`
    58→		rs.rule_id,
    59→		rs.segment_key,
    60→		s.match_type AS segment_match_type,
    61→		c.id AS constraint_id,
    62→		c."type" AS constraint_type,
    63→		c.property AS constraint_pro

   100→	rules, err := e.store.GetEvaluationRules(ctx, storage.NewResource(r.NamespaceKey, r.FlagKey))

   133→				e.logger.Debug(reason)
   134→				segmentKeys = append(segmentKeys, k)
   135→				segmentMatches++
   136→			}
   137→		}
   138→
   139→		switch rule.SegmentOperator {
   140→		case flipt.SegmentOperator_OR_SEGMENT_OPERATOR:
   141→			if segmentMatches < 1 {
   142→				e.logger.Debug("did not match ANY segments")
   143→				continue
   144→			}
   145→		case flipt.SegmentOperator_AND_SEGMENT_OPERATOR:

## Implementation Plan Summary

**Goal**: Add a `segment_match_type` field to `VariantEvaluationResponse` that shows whether segment matching used ALL or ANY logic.

### Key Findings:
1. **Proto location**: Field should be added to `VariantEvaluationResponse` in `/workspace/rpc/flipt/evaluation/evaluation.proto` with tag 10 (next available)
2. **Segment operator mapping**:
   - `OR_SEGMENT_OPERATOR` (value 0) → "ANY"
   - `AND_SEGMENT_OPERATOR` (value 1) → "ALL"  
   - No match → "" (empty string)

2. **Generated code** (`evaluation.pb.go`): Manually add field and getter method following existing string field patterns
3. **Server code** (`evaluation.go`): Enhance `variant()` method to fetch rules and populate `segment_match_type`

# Plan: Add segment_match_type Field to Flipt Evaluation Responses

## Context

Operators have requested that evaluation responses include a `segment_match_type` field showing whether an evaluation matched using ALL (all constraints matched) or ANY (at least one constraint matched) logic. This information already exists in the evaluation flow (in the EvaluationRule's SegmentOperator field in the storage layer) but is not exposed in responses.

## Requirements

1. Add `string segment_match_type` field to `VariantEvaluationResponse` proto message (tag 10)
2. Manually add corresponding field and getter method to generated Go code
3. Populate field in server code based on the matched rule's segment operator
4. Value should be "ALL", "ANY", or "" (empty when no segment matched)
5. Changes must span both proto and Go files (cross-language change)
6. Code must compile and tests must pass

- Getter methods: `GetFieldName()` pattern
